<Review>I've never used a moving service before, so I am not able to compare OCD with other companies, but I could not recommend OCD more highly. I wish I could give them six stars. This was a nerve-wracking move for me, going from my home of 18 years Oakland to Sacramento where I don't know anyone (moving for a job), and I basically only had one day to pack my one-bedroom apartment, so I was only about 85% ready when OCD arrived. The OCD guys (3 guys, TJ, Pasquale, and John K., the team leader) arrived 10 min. early and started working while I and my friends finished packing. This end of things took about an hour longer than the estimated time. Now, the apartment building where I was moving in Sacto has a policy where you have to pay $40/hr for a security guard while you are moving in. The OCD guys had been doing a great job moving my sometimes odd and haphazardly packed items, going at a steady pace, constantly communicating about where I wanted things, on target for expected timing on the load out, not slow or fast. Then, at 5:30 the security guard said he had to leave at 6 or he'd have to charge me time and a half. John said he'd never heard of a tenant having to pay to move into a place, and was (I felt, on my behalf) upset to hear I'd be charged extra. He and his crew put on the rocket boosters and finished up an hour's worth of unloading in 30 minutes. Their display of commitment to customer service and effort to minimize my costs was remarkable. I am so grateful to Daniel for his good (and reassuring) communication in advance of the move, and to John K., TJ and Pasquale for their stellar work moving my household. They made a difficult move go as smoothly as possible.<//Review><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Resp>

<rate>4</rate>< Review>
First time here and I think this place is pretty good over all. There is plenty of parking in the shared shopping center lot. We were seated quickly and service was fast. They no longer offer all you can eat sushi, via a paper notice on their door(bummer) but for about the same you would spend on all you can eat you still get a good amount and filled up by ordering by the roll. The staff are up beat and friendly and prices are fair. I really enjoyed "the diamond bar" roll. I'd come here again. For sure.</Review>

Food is often very good quality and menu is quite vast. Disappointed to learn that they no longer offer AYCE (all you can eat) sushi. Each sushi platter ranges between $5-$18 depending on whether you order sashimi, nigri, simple rolls, or specialty rolls. You can still order enough rolls to be full and satisfied for $40 or so. Staff is also very friendly. "Happy hour" specials seem to last all day and vary each day.</Text>

- Calamari Rings (Rubbery, hard to chew through)

My coworkers and I went here for lunch today, we're fortunate enough to be walking distance to this place. The restaurant has a lot of seating both at the bar and at the tables. For lunch, this place is not very crowded which works in our favor seeing how we have a one hour lunch. It's $21.95 for lunch, which is a bit more expensive than other AYCE lunch places, BUT the quality makes up for it here at Fusion 2. We ate at the bar and primarily ordered nigiri, don't know how their rolls or appetizers are (besides the calamari rings).

< review>
I happened to stumble upon this place by chance - I was supposed to meet a friend from out of town  who was delayed. I was super hungry and saw that Fusion 2 Any 1 was in the same shopping plaza as the It's A Grind coffee house that was our rendezvous point.

This is one of those moments when you feel as if you've found a gem. As a city boy, I'm used to higher prices and smaller portions (and lower quality, in some cases). And AYCE sushi always leaves me wary, especially buffet style. However, my expectations were upended in the most awesome way. The lunchtime price of $24 bucks gets you satisfying made-to-order AYCE sushi. With a drink included. And ice cream. !!!

My order consisted of a spicy 4-piece Tokyo Roll, an 8-piece Unagi roll, an 8-piece spicy tuna roll, 2 pieces of tuna sushi, and 2 pieces of Unagi sushi. The Tokyo had a nice kick to it though the fish on top was a little dry. The spicy tuna roll was PACKED with fish; the most I'd ever seen. The Unagi roll and sushi were tasty and generously sized. Lesser places have eel that tastes off - like dirty water - and drown the eel in sauce. Here, the eel was tender, mild, and just darn good. The tuna sushi was decent, too. A la carte, these items would total about $40.

The service was just fall-over-oneself wonderful. Seriously. It was almost too much! The sushi chefs and servers greet everyone as they come in. And two people ended up taking care of me while I was there sitting at the bar. They were so attentive, polite, and professional. Really, everyone was so nice.

This review is from an uncrowded weekend lunch experience. But between the solid sushi, extremely polite and welcoming staff, and fantastic AYCE quality-for-the-price that includes a soda and ice cream, a 5-star rating is a no-brainer. I'm rarely ever (never?) In San Dimas, but if you find yourself here or are in neighboring areas looking for a good AYCE sushi place, this place is definitely worth trying.< /review>

<Rating>4<//Rating><Text>I like this store! Today I bought fuel additive, with a dozen more to choose from. I've gotten good service from the staff, they are usually knowledgeable and helpful. I stopped there a few months ago because the check motor light came on. The gentleman plugged in his diagnostic tool and told me there was a problem with the catalytic converter or the sensors (2) that mesure the amount of oxygen going through the system. He then offered to look up the cost of the sensors as well as a new converter. I knew it wasn't the catalytic converter for it wouldn't run correctly. He then suggested I could use a fuel system additive that would turn off the check motor light, and if it turned off, its the sensors. I followed his recommendation and sure enough the light didn't come on again. All in all a good place to go for your car needs. They also lend tools to fix your car right there in the lot. 5<//rating>
< Text>
Burbank is not known for having latin food because theres not much to choose from. But with luck, I stumbled upon  this pupuseria. Tucked in on victory, right between a yatch shop and mechanic shop is a place where you can go and satisfy your salvadorian cravings but in exchange, you have to struggle with parking. The food is done from scratch and as you know, great food takes time. So if you're  in a time crunch, I would suggest to call the order in(they have delivery as well). They have a large selection of authentic salvadorian dishes. From pupusas, cheese oozing out on one side and crunchy golden brown burnt cheese on the other. Served with fresh and crisp cultido (pickled cabbage) which you can never have enough. Crispy Yucca frita, steaming hot served with  soft and chewy carnitas.  Atol de elote (sweet corn atole) served with a sweet corn on the cob on the side so you can personally scrape the corn into your rich and creamy drink. Fried  Platanos fritos that always seem to be ripe perfectly. They have a small selection of beer both American and imported.  Fresh agua frescas and horchata. Basically,You can't go wrong with anything on the menu. The server is friendly and is flexible to most special request. It is definitely worth visiting if you're around burbank and in the mood for a salvadorian experience.<//Text>

A friend recommended it to me because he knows I love cheese burgers. The first thing I noticed when we walked in was the temperature in the restaurant, warm. If the A/C was on it was set pretty high. Very stuffy stagnate air in the dinning area. Was greated by a friendly women who I assumed was a manager or shift leader because she was wearing a different colored shirt than everyone else. I ordered the sesonal item, Santa Barbara Char burger. Comes with 2 burger patties both topped with cheddar cheese and grilled onions, lettuce, tomatoes, pickles and avocado. I also got an order of fries, well done,  because lets be honest, fries are never as crispy as they should be because restaurants are in such a hurry to get food out. Also ordered the tempura green beans. My friend got the single char with swiss, grilled onions and lettuce. He's kind of a plain guy, I always say you can tell a lot about a person by how they order a cheese burger. Anywho my Santa Barbara burger was good the patties were seasoned properly the cheese was perfectly gooey, melty, the grilled onions were ok. Not as carmelized as they could be in my opinion. The Santa Barbara char comes on grilled bread not your traditional hamburger bun. All in all a pretty good burger. It just still has that synthetic fast food feel about it. No home made love feel like I get at In n Out or Riders Club. The fries were cooked well as I ordered them but you could tell they were frozen. Definitely not In n Out fresh cut quality. The tempura green beans were good. But for $2.99 I feel like we should have got more than what they gave us, kinda stingy if you know what I mean. Drink selection was good. I'm an iced tea guy so it was pretty cool they had three fresh brewed teas to choose from, black tea, tropical tea and a citrus green tea. Also had strawberry limeade which was pretty good. <UserId.>109128655814929790511<//UserId.><user_name>Eric Miller< /user_name>< Date>
1496975970217<//Date>
< rating>
3<//rating>
< Text>
First time to eat at The Habit today. A friend recommended it to me because he knows I love cheese burgers. The first thing I noticed when we walked in was the temperature in the restaurant, warm. If the A/C was on it was set pretty high. Very stuffy stagnate air in the dinning area. Was greated by a friendly women who I assumed was a manager or shift leader because she was wearing a different colored shirt than everyone else. I ordered the sesonal item, Santa Barbara Char burger. Comes with 2 burger patties both topped with cheddar cheese and grilled onions, lettuce, tomatoes, pickles and avocado. I also got an order of fries, well done,  because lets be honest, fries are never as crispy as they should be because restaurants are in such a hurry to get food out. Also ordered the tempura green beans. My friend got the single char with swiss, grilled onions and lettuce. He's kind of a plain guy, I always say you can tell a lot about a person by how they order a cheese burger. Anywho my Santa Barbara burger was good the patties were seasoned properly the cheese was perfectly gooey, melty, the grilled onions were ok. Not as carmelized as they could be in my opinion. The Santa Barbara char comes on grilled bread not your traditional hamburger bun. All in all a pretty good burger. It just still has that synthetic fast food feel about it. No home made love feel like I get at In n Out or Riders Club. The fries were cooked well as I ordered them but you could tell they were frozen. Definitely not In n Out fresh cut quality. The tempura green beans were good. But for $2.99 I feel like we should have got more than what they gave us, kinda stingy if you know what I mean. Drink selection was good. I'm an iced tea guy so it was pretty cool they had three fresh brewed teas to choose from, black tea, tropical tea and a citrus green tea. Also had strawberry limeade which was pretty good. In the end I would eat here again if I was in the area and didn't want to wait the 15 minutes it would take to get to In n Out.</Text>

They also give half patty on the Santa Barbara style instead of full meat patty... that was just a rip off. What I liked about this place... seating area outside.< /review>< pics>
